< text>
I have had severe neck pain for over 11 years from a work accident.  I never thought I would get any relief from the pain.  I had numbness in my fingers on and off.

My attorney sent me to Dr. Pablo Pazmino, in his Glendale office.

After fighting workers comp for about 2 years, I was finally approved for "Neck Fusion Surgery" in my C5-C6-C7 area of my neck.

I was nervous about anyone touching my neck, but I spoke to others, who my attorney also sent to Dr. Pazmino, so that made me feel better that they were very happy with their surgeries.  My wife had a "Disc Replacement" surgery done by Dr. Pazmino last year and had great success.

I went in on a Friday morning for surgery. When I awoke from my surgery, I was amazed that I was not in the severe pain I was before going into surgery.  I thought, well, maybe it was the pain medication, but I stopped the pain medications in less that 2 days after surgery and I had NO PAIN!

Even the incision in the front of my neck was not painful at all.

I had some swelling in my neck at my incision site, but all I did was ice it and it went down.

Dr. Pazmino told me that there was additional damage in my neck than what the MRI showed, but he was able to fix all that in this surgery.

2 weeks after surgery and I have been pain free since I awoke from the surgery! I have more range of motion in my neck, then I did PRIOR to my surgery.

Any surgery is scary.  Neck surgery is VERY scary.  While I was nervous going into surgery, I am AMAZED that I am no longer in pain and I am able to move my neck around.

I HIGHLY recommend him if you need neck surgery.  He has answered EVERY question and concern I had.  He called me the day before surgery, to check on any questions I had prior to surgery. He discussed it again before I was wheeled into the operating room.  He called me a few days later after surgery, to check on me.  I have never felt more comfortable in dealing with a surgeon.< /text>

< text>
Innovative, skillful spine surgeon with a big caring heart.
(Edited 12/10/2019)

I had a severe central stenosis and grade-one (light) disk dislocation in my L4-L5 spine. I had a debilitating sciatica at worst needing wheelchair. A well known orthopedic surgeon recommended standard laminectomy and fusion. I sought second opinion from Dr.Pazmino and he explained clearly in details and recommended a less invasive procedure: L4s + L5s bilateral hemilaminotomy foraminotomy Baxano (io-Flex) decompression and L45 Coflex inter-spinal insertion. This would spare my facet joints and also spare me from spinal fusion and promote quick recovery. I had my surgery in September 2015 by Dr. Pazmino. I had a speedy recovery. I started to walk with no leg pain in two weeks, resuming my 2-mile hiking in 6 weeks after. My back and legs were fully rejuvenated after 3 months. Meanwhile, I was under Dr. Pazmino's annual monitor for 2 years until release. Each passing year I am thankful to him that my back has been rejuvenated and trouble free, now, 2019, passing 4 years.
Dr. Pazmino cares a lot for his patient, whenever you have a health question, even unrelated to spine, he somehow responded to help promptly, through e-mail in my case. With currently increasingly more difficult to access your doctors through multi-layered gate-keepers (bots and human) of the physician or hospital networks, Dr. Pazimino is truly exceptional.

The following was the original posting I made in 2017:

My sciatica pain radiating to my leg started about two years prior to surgery and soon after I recovered and able to function until I unawarely reinjured my back after a hard gymn workout less than one year later. My sciatica became debilitating. A well known orthopedic surgeon (one of the top 25 nationally cited in 2015) diagnosed that I had a severe central stenosis and grade-one (light) disk shift in my L4-L5. Physical therapy and nerve root injection did not solve my problem. The doctor then recommended L4-L5 laminectomy and fusion. I was exploring for a less invasive procedure. I consulted Dr. Pazmino for a second opinion. Dr. Pazmino was one of a few surgeons practicing minimally invasive procedure in Southern California. He patiently and clearly explained my symptoms and recommended a less invasive io-Flex stenosis decompression and Coflex interspinal insert for my shift disk. I was out of hospital two days after surgery. I started to walk with no leg pain in two weeks. I resumed my light 2-mile hiking the 6th week after. My back and legs were fully rejuvenated after 3 months.
Dr. Pazmino did annual post surgery monitor for two years before releasing me. I am 75 year-old. The surgery, Tai Chi, Yoga and gymn exercises have rejuvenated my life. Thanks to Dr. Pazmino's skillful hands.< /text>

The food and atmosphere is 5 stars. Its a small family style seating place. But the service needs work. There is no actual leadership or  organized rhythm/plan for servicing customers. The people are friendly, hard working and good natured, but the food comes out slow and the servers are all over the place. It wasn't just me. I witnessed this with other customers around me. Overall, its still my favorite place for sushi. The prices and choices are great!<//text>

< Text>
This is a Hot Pastrami.
Maybe my hand is just small, but these sandwiches are a pretty good size. Nicely toasted bread. There's melted cheese on the bottom, then the meat, shredded lettuce, tomatoes and onions.
Top half of the sandwich has red wine vinaigrette.
This is one of the best pastrami sandwiches I've ever had. Its not bland, there is flavor in every bite including the meat by itself. I love that the pepperoncinis are already in it, usually its upon request, or on the side. Very good local place. Been here a few times. Definitely recommend for a good tasting sandwich.<//Text>

< review>
Was passing through and thought an italian sandwich sounded good. This place is not too far from the 101, so headed over. Its a relatively small place and decorated very italian. The lady the took my order was very nice. I decided on a half hot pastrami sandwich, a macaroni salad side, and a cannoli. It was not a long wait before I got my food.
I started eating it right away.  The half sandwich is pretty small which would have been ok if it made up in tastiness. It didn't.  Flavors ok. But the meat was tough and hard. Very tough to eat. Definitely over cooked. And they included a whole peppercini pepper! Should have been slices throughout so you get it throughout the sandwich. The only thing good about the sandwich was the bread. I have never had a hot pastrami like that.
Next, the macaroni salad. WAY too much mayo. And to me it was bland. I only got the mayo taste, nothing else.
Lastly, the cannoli. I have had many cannolis around the USA and even Italy. Need to take a cannoli class. Bland, no flavor whatsoever. I looked at it right when i got in my vegicle and it already had watery substance in it. Sgould necer happen to a cannoli when someone first receives it. A true cannoli should be creamy with italian goodness. Not sure what this was.
Even got a second opinion and they agreed with me on all the food. Completely disappointed. Will not be back. Waste of my money.</review>

<review>Talk about a tempting place to eat. Papa Napoli's is a family-owned business that makes their meatballs and sauce on Mondays. They do a lot of pre prep for the week on Mondays and the entire strip mall they're located in smells like meatballs and sauce and deliciousness. Their sauce is traditionally a thinner sauce with stronger basil and oregano taste to it. It is delightful but I am more fond of the thicker style. They are known for their hot pastrami sandwich.. I haven't tried it yet but I hear that it's wonderful. I guess that's a reason to come back and try the restaurant again when I'm in town. I did try their cannoli and it was good. The shell wad premade and it would have been nice had the chocolate chips been a little smaller but it was tasty nonetheless. < Review>
I have been going to car doctor for about 20 years, now.  Way back then, I realized, their foremost concern is safety.  If your ride isn't safe, neither are you!  This last time, my O2 sensor was causing the check engine light to go on.  I was a gearhead growing up, and they are aware of this.  When I called, Chris first advised me on some service I myself could do, with the hope we could address this in a more cost efficient manner.  When that didn't work, I took my van in and with more diagnostic work, they were able to take care of my issue quickly and pretty economically.
My job takes me all over CA and beyond.  I need my van to be reliable so that I can go on the road in a moments notice.  Car Doctor gives me the peace of mind to get on the road and return safely.  In the end, isn't that what we all want?< /Review>

<Text>Nothing can be as frightening as going to the mechanic when something is wrong with your car. After all, you drive your car nearly every day. And, of course, it is a huge investment. The fear of "crooked mechanics" is often based upon personal experience and personal pain.

However, the good reviews of The Car Doctor are very accurate. The people working on your vehicle will treat it with the same care and love as they would their own.

I wholeheartedly recommend The Car Doctor! After two separate experiences at their location, I'm convinced that they are honest and accurate. I'm not alone: I listened to others while I was waiting to drop off or pick up my vehicles. They treated my two Ford SUVs with the same care for which they treated some premium and luxury vehicles that they were working on.

Like many people, I've had some bad experiences with mechanics. I've experienced what happens when you take your car to a dealership and  the mechanics suddenly find different things that are "wrong" -- expensive things that still don't fix the car.

The guys at The Car Doctor are not like that. They quickly determined what was wrong. They quickly fixed it and for less than what the dealerships charge.

It almost sounds disingenuous for someone to say that they "trust" a mechanic. However, I actually trust the guys at The Car Doctor. If you're looking for a mechanic that you can entrust your vehicle with, then I wholeheartedly suggest these guys!

LOCATION: They are located in Palo Alto on San Antonio Road near the intersection with Middlefield.<//Text></record></dataset><record>

<rating>5< /rating>< Text>
I got a car after starting to work in the Bay Area.  I remember the first 3-4 years when I wandered around different dealerships and auto-repair shops recommended by my friends.  They may/may not have done a good job, may/may not be good value, but I am not sure if any of them really had my best interest at heart.

It is different with the Car Doctor.  They take care of your car, and they also take care of your wallet.  They've told me that some of the rickety-ness on my 8 y/o Corolla is not safety threatening so don't worry ; they've told me to delay changing brakes/tires because it is still safe to go for another 5000-7000 miles based on my usage pattern; then when the time came, they actually told me that Costco happens to have a great Michelin tire deal at that time and I should go there.

So when they say something "is" required, I listen.  For instance they probably recommend oil change slightly more frequently than what's advised for synthetic oil.  But that is because they want my CRV to go 500k miles. (apparently that is very doable) (and for any lingering doubters, there's barely any profit margin for oil change)

It has been about 7 years since my first visit.  I've moved from Mountain View, to Santa Clara, and now to East San Jose, but I continue to make the trek (ok, drive) to the Car Doctors every 6-9 months, for both my car and my wife's car, to have them maintain it.

As I gain my years in adult life, I found out that finding someone who has both good skills AND a good heart is an exceeding rarity.  I would wholeheartedly say that the Car Doctor is one of these rare finds, and they deserve every star on their Yelp (and now Google) review.<//Text>

<Review>The good: the atmosphere was great. Lots of little decorations added to the Peruvian and nautical themes. There is a wall containing white on dark grey writing that looks nearly identical to a wall in Mochica in San Francisco. Maybe both places were designed by the same person? The layout is interesting. Two floors; top has traditional dining while the bottom has club seating. Both floors have  bars, but the top floor bar is sparse. There are gas fire pits outside.

The bad: lighting outside is inadequate. Especially in the dark it is easy to pass by without knowing the restaurant was there. There are also not enough lights illuminating the walkway into the restaurant. The parking lots are small and cramped. The food was average. No great flavors or anything to really say I enjoyed.<//Review>< Pics>

< review>
We had reservations for 8:00pm in the evening. Parking was unbelievably difficult. If you park in the Northermost lot, be cautious about getting there as cars scrape their bottom on the little ramp.The restaurant in an acoustical nightmare. Bring earplugs if you find loud crescendos bouncing off windows and walls swirling around you disorienting. Earplugs help slightly. This was the worst atmosphere I have ever endured in a restaurant. I usually walk out of loud places, however we had family visiting from out of town and were hungry. The food was really amazing. Yes, it was really good and there are many reviews that say so. This is to warn people that might be traumatized by loud and constant noise that the weekend is definitely not the time to go. I would like to go back for the food, but I may have to see if they have a to-go menu.< /review>

< Text>
We have been to La Costanera a number of times and while it has always been good enough to not complain about, it has never been good enough to rave about.  The food has always been a plus while the actual restaurant and the service would leave a bit to be desired. Unfortunately, that was the case until last Saturday night.

We made reservations for 2 for a relaxed anniversary dinner as we didn't want to splurge for the Four Seasons and were in the mood for their Peruvian menu.  I'm going to keep it to an outline to avoid going on and on and to keep my irritation at a minimum.
- We were sat at approximately 6:50 pm at a table for 2.  Both an empty 4 top and a 2 top were next to us.
- At 7pm (10 min wait) I grabbed a busboy and requested water...he brought over chips and forgot the water, I re-requested & he brought a pitcher over. I let him know that we'd like to order drinks.
-At 7:05 (15 min wait), after watching both the 4 top and the 2 top get seated, I flag down the hostess who had originally sat us and let her know "please let your manager know that I've been waiting for 15 minutes without being greeted and I'm pissed."  Yes, it was probably a bit too aggressive, but it was honest.
-We wait for 5 more minutes while no one comes over to us
-7:10 (20 minutes of no service) - I walk to the front and tell the hostess that we still hadn't been seen and that I was ready to walk out.
7:12 Now the whole crew bursts to life.  I see the hostess talking to a server and the manager.  A different server approaches, apologizes for a mix up, and takes a drink order.  Then the manager comes over and offers a big apology and a free drink.

The rest of the evening was fine, I got over my seething anger, my dinner was decent (paella), my wifes was fantastic (ahi tuna), and we have a nice time.  My real problem boils down to the time from 7pm - 7:10.  Everyone makes mistakes and forgets a table...but when I specifically asked for help and then had to wait for 10 more minutes and ask a 2nd time?  That's just stupid.  Maybe I needed to leave my black card or keys on the table to let them know I could afford a nice meal, who knows.  I won't as I won't be going back.

The restaurant is loud and crowded.  The food is good, but not worth the trouble in my opinion.

PS - Parking is awful!  If you have a sedan or sports car, beware their extended lot that will absolutely rake the bottom of your car.  This time I parked across the street...loved running across PCH with my wife in the dark (/sarcasm).</Text>

<rate>5</rate>< text>
After reading other reviews, it looks like this place has been going through quite a bit of turmoil recently. On my first visit, however, everything was spot on: the food, the service, and the atmosphere--all excellent.

The food: I had the Ahi Tuna which was cooked and served just right, all in a picture-perfect presentation. I also tried the Adobo and shared the green salad, scallops, and Yucca balls--I recommend them all. Portions were moderately-sized, not huge but enough. Also shared a pitcher of sangria which went well with everything.

The service: Excellent. Our server was attentive and knowledgeable.

The atmosphere: I saw so many reviews of people complaining of coldness that I thought I might need to dress like an Eskimo. Temperature was right-on, but I can imagine sitting against a window may get a bit of a chill (we were in the middle). The decor is sleek and modern, which some people interpret as "cold" but I thought it looked great.

Definitely need to return when the sun is out longer--it was pitch black outside so the view was non-existent except for the brightly-lit hillside the restaurant was perched upon. I can imagine the view would be spectacular during the Summer.

As for all the other negative reviews... either we got lucky or the bugs have been ironed out. Everything was great.< /text>

<userid>107767768560438055175<//userid>< name>
Samantha Berg< /name>
< date>
1454090086573< /date>
<rating>4</rating>< Review>
Pleasantly surprised by my dinner here the other night.

We came as a group of 12 as part of a company offsite. The restaurant was incredibly accommodating and had set aside a large table for us. We had one person order for the entire group and the server was great in terms of making sure we had enough food and telling us how many of each item were in a plate so we could order accordingly. We shared a ton of plates:

Yucca balls - the server told us there were three to an order, but we actually had four on each plate. Creamy yucca with a crisp fry on the outside, serviced with a light curry sauce to add some spice and depth to the heaviness of the yucca root. 5-stars.

Pork belly skewers - pork belly is usually an easy win for me, but these tasted like burnt grill flavor, not fatty delicious pork. 3-stars.

Ceviche pescado -  not fishy at all, fabulous kick, loved the creamy sweet potato on the side. 5-stars.

Ceviche mixto - normally a win for me as I love seafood more than straight fish, but for this, I found the fish in the pescado ceviche soaked up the sauce better, while the seafood here remained somewhat unflavored. I did appreciate the variety of seafood here, with two shrimps, a mussel, a clam, some squid, and some fish. 3-stars.

Chicken chicharrones - crispy fried chicken, not the most moist I've ever had but still tenderly delicious, served with a thousand island type sauce on the side. 4-stars.

Beef empanadas - different flavor profile than I'm used to, tasted like chili in a buttery flaky crust. Super delicious, 5-stars.

Pulpo a la Parilla - not big pieces of octopus, as expected, but seemed more squid sized. Heavy grill flavor, but not burnt, and a little rubbery on the texture but still had good flavor. 4-stars.

Camarones - large and juicy with flavorful tomato sauce, and very garlicky bread. Lots of sauce, required extra bread! The bread was perfectly crisp and burned on one side, still fluffy inside. 4-stars.

Lamb Riblettes - suuuuuuper tender and fatty. Four to a serving. Yummmmmm 5-stars.

Lomo Saltado - Traditional, nice darker flavors from the soy in the tomato sauce. A good mix of potato softness and crunchiness on the fries.

The only issue we had was when we went to order cocktails, we were told there was no bartender so we had to stick to beer or wine.

Overall, really delicious, especially for the area!< /Review>
